Other Events. <br/></span></div><div style="text-indent:36pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">On July 1, 2025, Bank of America Corporation (the &#8220;Corporation&#8221;) issued a press release (&#8220;Press Release&#8221;) announcing that the Corporation plans to increase its quarterly common stock dividend from $0.26 per share to $0.28 per share beginning in the third quarter of 2025. The quarterly common stock dividend is subject to approval by the Corporation&#8217;s Board of Directors.</span></div><div><span><br/></span></div><div style="text-indent:36pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">The Press Release also announced the results of the Federal Reserve Board&#8217;s 2025 Comprehensive Capital Analysis and Review (&#8220;CCAR&#8221;). Under current Federal Reserve Board rules, the Corporation&#8217;s preliminary stress capital buffer (&#8220;SCB&#8221;) would improve 70 bps to 2.5%, and its CET1 minimum requirement would be 10.0%, effective October 1, 2025. To the extent the Federal Reserve Board&#8217;s recently proposed modifications to the SCB calculation are adopted as proposed, the Corporation&#8217;s 2025 stress test results would indicate an SCB of 2.7%, which would make its new CET1 minimum ratio 10.2%, effective January 1, 2026. At March 31, 2025, the Corporation had $201 billion of regulatory CET1 capital and a CET1 ratio of 11.8%, which exceeds the current minimum requirement.</span></div><div><span><br/></span></div><div style="text-indent:36pt"><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">A copy of the Press Release is attached hereto as Exhibit 99.1 and incorporated by reference into this Item 8.01.</span></div><div><span><br/></span></div><div><span style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Item 9.01. <title>Document</title></head><body><div id="i80e9e240ed2a40d4971a76a2fb0d75af_1"></div><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div style="text-align:right"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Exhibit 99.1 </font></div><div style="text-align:right"><img alt="logo.jpg" src="logo.jpg" style="height:41px;margin-bottom:5pt;vertical-align:text-bottom;width:284px"></div></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">July 1, 2025</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font style="background-color:#ffffff;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:14pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Bank of America Comments on Stress Test Results&#59;</font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font style="background-color:#ffffff;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:14pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Plans to Increase Quarterly Dividend 8% to $0.28 Per Share</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">CHARLOTTE, NC &#8211; Bank of America today commented on the results of the Federal Reserve&#8217;s 2025 Comprehensive Capital Analysis and Review (CCAR) and announced plans to increase its quarterly common stock dividend to $0.28 per share beginning in the third quarter of 2025.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The 2025 stress test results indicated that Bank of America&#8217;s modeled capital depletion improved 100 bps to 170 bps. Capital depletion measures the difference between a firm&#8217;s CET1 capital ratios at the beginning and in the most stressed period of the test scenario. As a result, under current Federal Reserve rules, Bank of America&#8217;s preliminary stress capital buffer (SCB) would improve 70 bps to 2.5%, and its CET1 minimum requirement would be 10.0%, effective October 1, 2025. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The Federal Reserve recently proposed modifications to the SCB calculation. If those rule changes are adopted as proposed, Bank of America&#8217;s 2025 stress test results would indicate an SCB of 2.7%, which would make its new CET1 minimum ratio 10.2%, effective January 1, 2026.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">At March 31, 2025, Bank of America had $201 billion of regulatory CET1 capital and a CET1 ratio of 11.8%, which exceeds the current minimum requirement.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The quarterly common stock dividend is subject to approval by Bank of America&#8217;s Board of Directors.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="background-color:#ffffff;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Forward-Looking Statements<br><br>Certain statements contained in this news release may constitute &#8220;forward-looking&#8221; statements within the meaning of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995. These forward-looking statements represent the current expectations, plans or forecasts of Bank of America based on available information. Forward-looking statements can be identified by the fact that they do not relate strictly to historical or current facts.
